# TODO

Project task tracking for aidevops framework.

Compatible with [todo-md](https://github.com/todo-md/todo-md), [todomd](https://github.com/todomd/todo.md), [taskell](https://github.com/smallhadroncollider/taskell), [Beads](https://github.com/steveyegge/beads), and TOON-enhanced parsing.

## Format

**Human-readable:**

```markdown
- [ ] tXXX Task description @owner #tag ~4h (ai:2h test:1h read:30m) logged:2025-01-15
  - [ ] tXXX.1 Subtask ~2h blocked-by:tYYY
    - [ ] tXXX.1.1 Sub-subtask ~1h
  - [ ] tXXX.2 Another subtask ~1h blocks:tZZZ
- [x] tYYY Completed task ~2h actual:1.5h logged:2025-01-10 completed:2025-01-15
- [-] tZZZ Declined task
```

**Task ID format:**

- `t001` - Top-level task
- `t001.1` - Subtask of t001
- `t001.1.1` - Sub-subtask of t001.1
- IDs are stable and never reused

**Dependency fields:**

- `blocked-by:t001,t002` - This task cannot start until t001 and t002 are done
- `blocks:t003,t004` - Completing this task unblocks t003 and t004
- `parent:t001` - This is a child of t001 (implicit from indentation)

**Time fields:**

- `~estimate` - Total time estimate with optional breakdown `(ai:Xh test:Xh read:Xm research:Xm)`
- `actual:` - Actual time spent (recorded at commit/release)
- `logged:` - When task was added
- `started:` - When branch was created (work began)
- `completed:` - When task was marked done

**Assignment fields:**

- `assignee:identity` - Who claimed the task (set by `supervisor-helper.sh claim`, identity = `AIDEVOPS_IDENTITY` or `user@host`)
- `@owner` - Who is responsible for the task (separate from assignee — future feature)

**Machine data:** TOON blocks in HTML comments (invisible when rendered).

<!--TOON:meta{version,format,updated}:
2.0,todo-md+toon+beads,2025-12-21T16:00:00Z
-->

- [x] t1699 fix: localdev ANSI escape codes corrupt Traefik route YAML files — `_cmd_branch_assign_port()` writes ANSI-colored `print_info`/`print_success` to stdout, then returns port via `echo`. - [x] t1430 Research rtk-ai/rtk CLI proxy for token reduction integration — evaluate [rtk](https://github.com/rtk-ai/rtk) (5.8k stars, MIT, Rust) as token-saving layer for aidevops. rtk is a CLI proxy that intercepts command outputs (ls, cat, grep, git, test runners) and compresses them before they reach the LLM context, claiming 60-90% token reduction with <10ms overhead. Single binary, zero dependencies. Assess: (1) compatibility with aidevops agent dispatch and worktree workflows, (2) integration points — does it complement or conflict with our existing file discovery rules (git ls-files, fd, rg), (3) cost savings projection based on observability metrics, (4) whether rtk's output filtering could break agent tool parsing (structured JSON outputs, error detection), (5) installation/deployment via setup.sh, (6) comparison with our prompt-level token discipline (build.txt rules). - [x] t1408 Recursive task decomposition for dispatch — classify/decompose pipeline inspired by [TinyAGI/fractals](https://github.com/TinyAGI/fractals). Add a pre-dispatch step that uses a cheap LLM call (haiku) to classify tasks as atomic or composite, then recursively decomposes composites into 2-5 independent subtasks with dependency edges. Includes lineage context passing (each worker gets ancestor chain + sibling descriptions to prevent scope drift and duplication). Three integration points: (1) interactive `/full-loop` and `/new-task` — show decomposition tree for user confirmation before dispatch, (2) pulse/supervisor — auto-decompose before dispatching, with depth limit (max 3) to prevent runaway recursion, (3) `/mission` — replace mission's milestone decomposition with the same classify/decompose pipeline for consistency. Batch execution strategies (depth-first default, breadth-first option) for rate-limit-aware parallel dispatch. #plan #feature #orchestration #decomposition #auto-dispatch ~10h (ai:7h test:2h read:1h) model:opus ref:GH#2983 logged:2026-03-06 completed:2026-03-07 -> [todo/PLANS.md#2026-03-06-recursive-task-decomposition]

- [x] t1363 Conversational memory and entity relationship system for multi-channel agents — three-layer architecture: Layer 0 (immutable raw interaction log across all channels), Layer 1 (per-conversation context with AI-judged idle detection replacing fixed timeouts), Layer 2 (entity relationship model with identity resolution across Matrix/SimpleX/email/CLI, inferred needs, expectations, capability gaps). Self-evolution loop: entity interaction patterns → gap detection → automatic TODO creation with evidence trail → system upgrade. Immutability principle: raw messages are append-only source of truth, all summaries/profiles/inferences are derived layers that reference back to source records. Privacy-aware context loading prevents cross-channel information leakage. Replaces deterministic thresholds (sessionIdleTimeout, prune age, dedup matching) with AI judgment calls. Model-agnostic: memory layer provides continuity regardless of which model handles the conversation. #plan #feature #memory #entity #communications #self-improvement ~27h (ai:20h test:4h read:3h) model:opus ref:GH#2518 logged:2026-02-27 -> [todo/PLANS.md#2026-02-27-conversational-memory-entity-relationship-system]

- [x] t1352 docs: Add Next.js stale lock file knowledge to local-hosting.md — Next.js 16+ creates a file-based lock at `apps/web/.next/dev/lock`. If the dev server is killed (`kill -9`, system restart, OOM), the lock file survives and blocks restart with `Unable to acquire lock`. Port-killing alone (`lsof -ti:PORT | xargs kill -9`) doesn't clean it up. Add to `services/hosting/local-hosting.md`: (1) document the lock file issue in the Next.js section, (2) recommend `rm -f apps/web/.next/dev/lock` before starting, (3) add recommended Tabby/terminal profile start command pattern that includes the lock cleanup. #docs #local-hosting #auto-dispatch ~15m model:sonnet ref:GH#2478 logged:2026-02-27 pr:#2482 completed:2026-02-27

- [x] t1314 Fix batch concurrency bypass when pulse runs without --batch flag — `cmd_pulse()` only uses batch concurrency when called with explicit `--batch <id>`. Without it, Phase 2 falls through to global dispatch with `SUPERVISOR_MAX_CONCURRENCY` (default: 4), ignoring the batch's `concurrency=1` setting. Five contributing causes: (1) no batch auto-detection in `cmd_pulse()`, (2) auto-batch absorption has no affinity checks, (3) `cmd_next()` sibling limits ignore batch concurrency, (4) `blocked-by:` not enforced in dispatch path, (5) AI lifecycle auto-merge has no human review gate. Fix: auto-detect active batches in `cmd_pulse()`, add batch affinity to auto-absorption, cap sibling limits to batch concurrency, persist `blocked-by:` in DB or re-check at dispatch time, require explicit opt-in for auto-merge. Affected files: `pulse.sh` (Phase 2), `cron.sh` (auto-pickup), `state.sh` (`cmd_next()`), `dispatch.sh` (concurrency check). ~8h (ai:6h test:2h) #bugfix #supervisor #auto-dispatch model:opus ref:GH#2163 logged:2026-02-23 pr:#2236 verified:2026-02-25 completed:2026-02-25

- [x] t1234 Fix cross-repo subtask creation — DB lookup must take priority over primary repo match to prevent task ID collision writing subtasks to wrong repo. When multiple repos have the same task ID (e.g., both have t003), `_exec_create_subtasks` finds the parent in the primary repo first and never reaches the cross-repo DB lookup. Fix: check supervisor DB for task's repo FIRST, only fall back to primary repo if DB has no record. Also add issue-sync guard to reject creating issues for tasks whose repo doesn't match the current repo. #bugfix #security #supervisor ~30m model:sonnet ref:GH#1895 pr:#1896 completed:2026-02-19
- [x] t1235 Fix issue-sync-helper.sh `cmd_push()` cross-repo vulnerability — same class of bug as t1234. `cmd_push()` (line ~1520) uses `detect_repo_slug("$project_root")` to determine which GitHub repo to create issues in. When the supervisor calls `cmd_push` from the aidevops repo directory but TODO.md contains tasks belonging to other repos (via cross-repo DB), all issues get created in the wrong repo. Fix: for each task being pushed, check the supervisor DB for the task's actual repo. If the task's repo doesn't match the current `repo_slug`, skip it (or push to the correct repo). Same pattern as the t1234 fix — DB is authoritative for task-to-repo mapping. #bugfix #security #issue-sync #auto-dispatch ~1h model:sonnet ref:GH#1909 assignee:marcusquinn started:2026-02-19T04:08:49Z pr:#1912 completed:2026-02-19

- [x] t1200 IP reputation check agent — vet VPS/server/proxy IPs before purchase/deployment. Create `tools/security/ip-reputation.md` agent and `ip-reputation-helper.sh` CLI that queries multiple IP reputation providers in parallel, merges results into a unified risk report, and caches in SQLite. Use case: before buying a VPS, dedicated server, or proxy pool, check if the IPs are already burned (blacklisted, flagged as spam/abuse/proxy/VPN, listed on DNSBLs). Follows the same orchestrator+provider pattern as tech-stack-helper.sh (t1063). Providers (all curl/DNS-queryable, no browser automation needed): (1) **IPQualityScore** (ipqualityscore.com) — fraud score, proxy/VPN/Tor detection, abuse velocity, bot detection. Free tier: 5000 lookups/month. REST API. (2) **Scamalytics** (scamalytics.com) — fraud score 0-100, proxy/VPN detection, ISP risk. Free tier available. Investigate API endpoints via network analysis of their web lookup tool to avoid browser automation. (3) **AbuseIPDB** (abuseipdb.com) — community-reported abuse, confidence score 0-100. Free: 1000 checks/day. REST API. (4) **ProxyCheck.io** (proxycheck.io) — proxy/VPN/Tor detection, risk score 0-100. Free: 1000 req/day, no key required. REST API. (5) **GreyNoise** (greynoise.io) — mass scanner/bot detection, malicious classification. Free: 10000 req/month. REST API. (6) **Spamhaus/DNSBL** — PBL/SBL/CBL/XBL via DNS lookup (dig reversed-ip.zen.spamhaus.org). Free for non-commercial. (7) **Shodan** (shodan.io) — open ports, hosting infra, known malicious services. Free tier. REST API. (8) **IP Hub** (iphub.info) — residential vs proxy/VPN classification. Free: 1000 req/day. (9) **StopForumSpam** (stopforumspam.com) — spammer IP database. Free API, no key. (10) **Blocklist.de** (blocklist.de) — attack/botnet IP feeds. Free API. Also integrate with existing `email-health-check-helper.sh blacklist` command for DNSBL overlap. Output: unified risk report with per-provider scores, overall risk rating (clean/low/medium/high/critical), VPN/proxy/Tor flags, blacklist hits, abuse reports, and recommendation (safe to use / proceed with caution / avoid). Commands: `ip-reputation-helper.sh check <ip>` (single IP), `ip-reputation-helper.sh batch <file>` (bulk from file, one IP per line), `ip-reputation-helper.sh report <ip>` (detailed markdown report), `ip-reputation-helper.sh providers` (list configured providers and API key status). Add `/ip-check <ip>` slash command. Re: Scamalytics API discovery — use browser dev tools or mitmproxy to capture the XHR/fetch calls their web lookup makes, then replicate with curl. Many "web-only" tools actually call a JSON API under the hood. Update subagent-index and AGENTS.md progressive disclosure table (Security domain). #feature #auto-dispatch #agent #security #infrastructure ~6h (ai:4h test:1.5h research:30m) model:sonnet ref:GH#1820 assignee:marcusquinn started:2026-02-20T17:45:10Z logged:2026-02-18 pr:#2020 completed:2026-02-20

- [x] t1071 Fix pulse Phase 3b2 crash on mergedAt:null — pulse.sh line 591 `pr_merged_at=$(echo "$pr_json" | grep -o '"mergedAt":"[^"]*"' | cut -d'"' -f4)` crashes the entire pulse when a PR has `"mergedAt":null` (not merged). The `grep -o` returns exit code 1 (no match), and `set -euo pipefail` kills the script. This prevents Phase 3.5 (rebase retry) and Phase 3.6 (opus escalation) from ever running, causing all merge-conflict blocked tasks to stall indefinitely. Fix: add `|| echo ""` after the grep, or use jq. Same pattern on line 590 for `pr_state` (less likely to fail but same risk). This is a critical bug — it's been silently killing the pulse for hours, preventing 5 PRs from being rebased. #bugfix #supervisor #critical #auto-dispatch ~15m model:sonnet ref:GH#1552 logged:2026-02-16 pr:#1553 completed:2026-02-17
- [x] t1070 Post blocked reason comment on GitHub issues when status:blocked is applied — `sync_issue_status_label()` in issue-sync.sh applies the `status:blocked` label but never posts a comment explaining why. The error reason is stored in the DB (`--error` arg to `cmd_transition`) but not surfaced on the issue. `post_blocked_comment_to_github()` already exists (t296) but is only called from `todo-sync.sh` when a worker self-reports blocked. - [x] t1011 Model contest mode — when model selection is uncertain, dispatch the same task to top-3 models in parallel, then have each model rank all outputs (including its own). Uses existing `response-scoring-helper.sh` (SQLite scoring DB, criteria: correctness 30%, completeness 25%, code quality 25%, clarity 20%) and `compare-models-helper.sh` (model specs). Flow: (1) supervisor detects uncertainty (no pattern data, new task type, or explicit `model:contest`), (2) dispatches 3 workers with same prompt to different models (e.g. opus, sonnet, gemini), (3) collects outputs, (4) sends all 3 outputs to each model for blind cross-ranking (outputs anonymised as A/B/C), (5) aggregates scores, picks winner, (6) records results in pattern-tracker and response-scoring DB, (7) applies winning output. Cost: ~3x a single run, but builds permanent routing data. Only trigger for genuinely uncertain cases — not every task. #feature #supervisor #self-improvement #auto-dispatch ~2h (ai:1h30m test:30m) model:opus ref:GH#1301 assignee:marcusquinn logged:2026-02-12 pr:#1344 completed:2026-02-13

- [x] t1008 Pre-dispatch reverification for previously-claimed tasks — when dispatching a task that was previously claimed (dead worker, unclaimed, re-queued), the supervisor should dispatch a lightweight verification-only worker instead of a full implementation worker. The verify worker's prompt: "Task t{id} was previously worked on. Check if the deliverable already exists and works: run tests, ShellCheck, verify integration. If complete, create a short verification PR or report back. If incomplete, continue implementation." This costs ~$0.10-0.20 (sonnet, small context) vs ~$1.00 for a full implementation session that discovers the work is done. The key insight: never trust file existence or merged PRs as proof — always reverify. - [x] t196 Fix RETURN trap clobbering in trap cleanup scripts #bugfix #quality #shell ~1h (ai:45m test:15m) ref:GH#815 assignee:marcusquinn started:2026-02-09T22:46:55Z logged:2026-02-09 completed:2026-02-09 pr:#827
  - Notes: CodeRabbit review on PR #801 (t135.9) identified that `trap 'rm -f "$tmp"' RETURN` clobbers existing RETURN traps and can fail with `set -u` when the local temp var goes out of scope. Pattern: `_prev=$(trap -p RETURN); trap 'rm -f "$tmp"; eval "$_prev"' RETURN`.

- [x] t189 Worktree ownership safety — prevent sessions from removing worktrees owned by other parallel sessions #bugfix #git #supervisor ~2h (ai:1.5h test:30m) ref:GH#692 assignee:marcusquinn started:2026-02-09T00:24:23Z logged:2026-02-09 completed:2026-02-09 verified:2026-02-09 PR #695 merged
  - [x] t189.1 Add worktree ownership registry ~45m blocked-by:none pr:#695
    - Notes: When a session creates or claims a worktree, register it in a SQLite table or lockfile: worktree path, session ID, PID, task ID, created timestamp. Before removing any worktree, check the registry — if another session owns it and its PID is still alive, REFUSE to remove. If PID is dead but session is recent (<1h), WARN and require --force. This prevents the exact bug that happened: supervisor session cleaned up a worktree that a parallel interactive session was actively using.
  - [x] t189.2 Add "in use" detection to worktree cleanup ~30m blocked-by:t189.1 pr:#695
    - Notes: Before `git worktree remove`, check: (1) is any process with CWD inside the worktree? (`lsof +D` or `fuser`), (2) is the worktree registered to another session?, (3) are there uncommitted changes? Only remove if all three are clear. Add --force to override (with warning). Wire into supervisor cleanup, `wt merge`, and any other worktree removal paths.
  - [x] t189.3 Add AGENTS.md rule: never remove worktrees you didn't create ~15m blocked-by:none pr:#695
    - Notes: Immediate instruction-level fix. Add to AGENTS.md: "NEVER remove a worktree unless (a) you created it in this session, (b) it belongs to a task you are managing, or (c) the user explicitly asks. Worktrees may belong to parallel sessions — removing them destroys another agent's working directory." This is the cheapest fix and should be done first.
  - [x] t189.4 Scope batch cleanup to batch-owned worktrees only ~30m blocked-by:none pr:#695
    - Notes: The supervisor's worktree cleanup during pulse should ONLY touch worktrees for tasks in the current batch. Currently it can discover and remove any worktree matching the naming pattern. Add batch_id filtering: only clean worktrees whose task_id is in the batch being pulsed.
  - Notes: Root cause from 2026-02-09: supervisor session force-removed a worktree (`bugfix/setup-template-opencode-install`) that belonged to a parallel interactive session. The branch survived but the other session lost its working directory and had to restart. Git workflow protects code (branches survive), but the worktree directory is the active workspace — losing it mid-session is disruptive. Three layers of fix needed: (1) instruction-level rule (t189.3, cheapest), (2) ownership registry (t189.1, most robust), (3) in-use detection (t189.2, defense in depth).

Root cause likely: dispatch command fails silently before worker starts (e.g. opencode binary not found, worktree creation fails, prompt too long). - [x] t167 Investigate Gemini Code Assist for full codebase review in daily pulse #quality #automation #research ~30m (ai:20m read:10m) ref:GH#625 assignee:marcusquinn logged:2026-02-08 started:2026-02-08 completed:2026-02-08 verified:2026-02-08 PR #650 merged
  - Notes: **Research complete (2026-02-08).** Gemini Code Assist GitHub bot (`gemini-code-assist[bot]`) only reviews PR diffs -- confirmed via official docs (developers.google.com/gemini-code-assist/docs/review-github-code, updated 2026-02-02). No full codebase review API or trigger exists. Commands limited to `/gemini review`, `/gemini summary`, `@gemini-code-assist` -- all PR-scoped. Consumer quota: 33 PR reviews/day; Enterprise: 100+/day. **Three approaches evaluated:**
  - **Option 1: Synthetic full-diff PR** -- Create branch from empty tree (`git commit-tree $(git hash-object -t tree /dev/null)`), PR against main. Forces Gemini to review entire codebase as a "diff". VIABLE but hacky: creates noise in PR history, may hit review size limits, 33/day consumer quota means 1 daily review is feasible. Recommended as interim approach for t166 integration.
  - **Option 2: Gemini CLI (gemini-cli)** -- Open-source CLI agent with ReAct loop, file read/write, MCP support. Free tier: 1000 requests/day, 60/min. Can be prompted to review codebase locally without GitHub bot. MOST VIABLE for daily pulse: run `gemini review the codebase for quality issues` in repo dir, parse structured output. No PR needed. Integrates via supervisor dispatch like any other CLI tool.
  - **Option 3: Gemini API directly** -- Use Gemini 3 Pro/Flash via API with 1M token context window. Feed repo contents, get structured review. VIABLE but requires API key management and custom integration code. Higher cost than CLI approach.
  - **Recommendation:** Option 2 (Gemini CLI) is the best path for t166 integration. It's free, local, scriptable, and avoids the PR-only limitation of the GitHub bot. Add as t166 subtask: `gemini-cli-helper.sh review` command that runs Gemini CLI codebase review, parses output into same structured format as CodeRabbit findings. Option 1 (synthetic PR) is a viable fallback if CLI output quality is insufficient. Option 3 is overkill for this use case.
  - **Quality assessment:** Gemini's review on PR #622 caught a real regex issue (high severity) but also produced false positives. Same bot-review verification rules from t166.2 apply. Gemini focuses on: correctness, efficiency, maintainability, security. Customizable via `.gemini/styleguide.md` (already have `.gemini/settings.json` in repo). Enterprise version supports cross-repo style guides via Google Cloud console.

Recommendation: No adoption needed. aidevops already implements the progressive disclosure pattern more robustly.

- [x] t060 Research jj (Jujutsu) VCS for aidevops advantages #research #git #tools ~15m (ai:10m read:5m) ref:GH#514 logged:2026-01-13 ref:https://github.com/jj-vcs/jj verified:2026-02-08
  - Notes: Git-compatible VCS (25.6k stars, v0.38.0, Apache-2.0, 300+ contributors, backed by Google). Written in Rust, uses gitoxide for Git backend. Key features: working-copy-as-commit (no staging area), operation log with full undo, conflicts as first-class objects, automatic rebase of descendants, anonymous branches (bookmarks), revset query language, safe concurrent replication.
  - Evaluation for aidevops:
    - RECOMMENDED: Colocated mode (`jj git init --colocate`) as bridge strategy. Maintains full git compatibility (all 39 scripts + 67 docs still work), allows gradual adoption, preserves GitHub/CI integration. jj and git commands work interchangeably in same repo.
    - HIGH VALUE: Operation log + undo eliminates the destructive command risk that spawned t009 (PreToolUse hooks). `jj undo` reverses any operation including the equivalent of `git reset --hard`. Would reduce need for pre-edit-check.sh defensive machinery (206 lines).
    - HIGH VALUE: jj workspaces (`jj workspace add`) are lighter than git worktrees. Could simplify the 3-tier fallback chain (wt -> worktree-helper.sh -> raw git worktree) in supervisor-helper.sh parallel dispatch.
    - MEDIUM VALUE: No staging area simplifies commit workflow. Working copy is always a commit, eliminating "dirty working copy" errors and `git stash` usage (7 files). Automatic rebase of descendants eliminates manual `git rebase main` after fetching (9 files).
    - MEDIUM VALUE: First-class conflicts enable committing conflicted state, resolving later. Valuable for supervisor parallel task dispatch where agents touch overlapping files. Conflict resolution propagates through descendants automatically.
    - MEDIUM VALUE: Change IDs persist through squash-merge/rebase/amend, solving the squash-merge detection problem in worktree-helper.sh `cmd_clean()` (currently uses fragile heuristics).
    - CONCERN: No git hooks support yet (issue #405). Pre-commit hooks are used by aidevops for quality gates. Workaround: run linters via jj's `run` command (design doc exists) or keep colocated mode where git hooks still fire.
    - CONCERN: No git submodules support yet. Not a blocker for aidevops (no submodules used).
    - CONCERN: No .gitattributes support (issue #53). Minor impact.
    - CONCERN: Still experimental (pre-1.0). Core devs use it daily, but storage format may change before 1.0. Colocated mode mitigates this -- can always fall back to pure git.
    - CONCERN: Learning curve for team. jj concepts (changes vs commits, bookmarks vs branches, revsets) differ from git mental model. Mitigated by colocated mode allowing gradual adoption.
  - Recommendation: Add jj as OPTIONAL tool in setup.sh alongside Worktrunk. Create a `tools/git/jj.md` subagent documenting jj equivalents for common aidevops git operations. Do NOT replace git -- use colocated mode as an enhancement layer. Revisit after jj 1.0 for deeper integration.
  - Follow-up tasks: t060.1 Add jj installation to setup.sh (optional), t060.2 Create tools/git/jj.md subagent, t060.3 Test jj colocated mode with supervisor parallel dispatch.

- [-] t099 ~~Add Neural-Chromium for agent-native browser automation~~ #tools #browser #ai #automation ~2h logged:2026-01-30 declined:2026-02-05
  - Notes: DECLINED - Neural-Chromium has only 4 stars, no releases, and is Windows-only. Not viable for macOS/Linux users. Better alternatives: browser-use (77.8k stars, cross-platform), Stagehand (20.8k stars, already documented), Skyvern (20.3k stars). The existing neural-chromium.md subagent should be removed. Features: 1.3s interaction latency (4.7x faster than Playwright), semantic DOM understanding via accessibility tree, VLM-powered vision (Llama 3.2 via Ollama), stealth capabilities (no navigator.webdriver), deep iframe access. Uses shared memory + gRPC for direct browser state access. Tools: click(element_id), type(element_id, text), observe() for DOM snapshots. Early stage but promising for agent automation. Evaluate for: CAPTCHA solving, dynamic SPA interaction, form filling. Add to tools/browser/ as experimental option.

  - Notes: Apple-inspired "Mom Test" framework for UX evaluation and CRO. **6 UX Principles:** Clarity, Simplicity, Consistency, Feedback, Discoverability, Forgiveness. **Workflow:** 1) Screen-by-screen "Would this confuse my mom?" analysis. 2) Generate tables: Confusing Element | Mom's Reaction | Fix. 3) Rank biggest UX failures by severity. 4) Identify quick wins with effort/impact matrix. 5) Prioritize CRO recommendations based on proven UX patterns. **Output:** Actionable report with specific fixes, not vague suggestions. - [x] t124 Add Tirith terminal security guard for homograph/injection attacks #security #tools #terminal ~20m (ai:15m test:3m read:2m) ref:GH#522 logged:2026-02-03 ref:https://github.com/sheeki03/tirith completed:2026-02-08 verified:2026-02-08 PR #605 merged
  - Notes: Tirith (1,300 stars, Rust, AGPL-3.0) - also see t104 plan: Tirith's `tirith run` command provides verified download-then-execute as the implementation vehicle for curl|sh hardening. - terminal security tool that catches attacks browsers block but terminals don't. **30 rules across 7 categories:** 1) Homograph attacks (Cyrillic/Greek lookalikes, punycode, mixed-script). 2) Terminal injection (ANSI escapes, bidi overrides, zero-width chars). 3) Pipe-to-shell (`curl|bash`, `wget|sh`, `eval $(wget ...)`). 4) Dotfile attacks (downloads targeting ~/.bashrc, ~/.ssh/authorized_keys). 5) Insecure transport (HTTP piped to shell, `curl -k`). 6) Ecosystem threats (git clone typosquats, untrusted Docker registries, pip/npm URL installs). 7) Credential exposure (userinfo tricks, shortened URLs). **Integration options:** 1) Add to aidevops setup/onboarding as recommended install. 2) Create tirith.md subagent at tools/security/. 3) Document shell hook setup (`eval "$(tirith init)"`). 4) Consider MCP wrapper for `tirith check` command validation. **Key features:** Sub-millisecond overhead, local-only (no network calls), YAML policy config, bypass with `TIRITH=0` prefix. Install: `brew install sheeki03/tap/tirith` or `npm install -g tirith` or `cargo install tirith`.

The pr_url field should be populated from the log even when the worker doesn't explicitly signal completion.

- [x] t215 Accessibility & contrast testing — WCAG compliance for websites + emails #plan #accessibility #testing #wcag → [todo/PLANS.md#2026-02-10-accessibility-contrast-testing] ~2.5h (ai:2h test:25m read:5m) ref:GH#903 assignee:marcusquinn started:2026-02-10T04:30:21Z logged:2026-02-10 completed:2026-02-10 pr:#919
  - [x] t215.1 Create services/accessibility/accessibility-audit.md — unified web + email accessibility agent ~15m ref:GH#904 assignee:marcusquinn started:2026-02-10T14:39:25Z completed:2026-02-10 pr:#932
    - Notes: Unified accessibility testing agent covering web pages and email HTML. Tool decision tree: axe-core (free, open-source, de facto standard — inject via Playwright page.evaluate or @axe-core/cli) for automated WCAG 2.2 A/AA rule checking. WAVE API (paid, $0.025-0.04/credit, 100 free credits) for comprehensive analysis with XPath/CSS selectors for each issue. WebAIM Contrast Checker API (free, no key) for individual color pair validation. Lighthouse accessibility category (already installed via pagespeed-helper.sh) for scoring + audit results. Covers: color contrast (WCAG 2.1 SC 1.4.3 AA 4.5:1 normal/3:1 large, SC 1.4.6 AAA 7:1/4.5:1, SC 1.4.11 non-text contrast 3:1), keyboard navigation, ARIA roles/labels, heading hierarchy, alt text, form labels, focus indicators, link purpose, language attributes, reading order, motion/animation preferences. Email-specific: table role=presentation, semantic headings in table cells, lang attribute on html element, link text quality (no "click here"), sufficient contrast in inline styles.
  - [x] t215.2 Create accessibility-audit-helper.sh — CLI wrapping axe-core, WAVE, WebAIM contrast, Lighthouse a11y ~25m ref:GH#905 assignee:marcusquinn started:2026-02-10T14:41:09Z completed:2026-02-10 pr:#935
    - Notes: Commands: audit (full WCAG scan via axe-core on URL or local file), contrast (extract all fg/bg color pairs from computed styles via Playwright, check against WCAG AA/AAA thresholds), contrast-check (single color pair via WebAIM API — fcolor, bcolor, returns ratio + AA/AAA pass/fail), wave (submit URL to WAVE API, parse errors/contrast/alerts/features/structure/ARIA), lighthouse-a11y (run Lighthouse --only-categories=accessibility, parse individual audits), email-a11y (axe-core + email-specific rules on HTML file), report (generate WCAG compliance report — pass/fail per success criterion, grouped by principle). Config: WAVE API key via aidevops secret, output format (json/markdown/html), WCAG level target (A/AA/AAA, default AA).
  - [x] t215.3 Playwright contrast extraction — computed style analysis for all visible elements ~20m ref:GH#906 assignee:marcusquinn started:2026-02-10T14:58:48Z completed:2026-02-10 pr:#937
    - Notes: Use Playwright page.evaluate() to traverse all visible DOM elements, extract computed foreground color (color) and background color (backgroundColor, walking up ancestors for transparent backgrounds), font size and weight (to determine "large text" threshold: >=18pt or >=14pt bold). Calculate contrast ratio per WCAG formula: (L1 + 0.05) / (L2 + 0.05) where L = relative luminance. Flag failures at AA (4.5:1 normal, 3:1 large) and AAA (7:1 normal, 4.5:1 large). Also check non-text contrast (SC 1.4.11) for UI components and graphical objects at 3:1. Handle edge cases: gradients (sample multiple points), background images (flag as manual review), opacity, CSS filters. Output: element selector, actual colors, computed ratio, threshold, pass/fail, WCAG criterion. Cross-validate individual pairs against WebAIM Contrast Checker API for accuracy.
  - [x] t215.4 WAVE API integration — comprehensive accessibility analysis ~15m ref:GH#907 assignee:marcusquinn started:2026-02-10T15:00:07Z completed:2026-02-10 pr:#941
    - Notes: WAVE API at wave.webaim.org/api/. Auth: API key parameter. Endpoints: /request with url + key + reporttype (1=basic stats, 2=detailed with selectors, 3=page source annotated, 4=full). Credits: reporttype 1-2 cost 1 credit, 3 costs 2, 4 costs 3. Response JSON: categories (error, contrast, alert, feature, structure, aria) each with count + items array. Items include id (rule code), description, count, selectors (XPath + CSS). Map WAVE rule IDs to WCAG success criteria for compliance reporting. Cache results to avoid burning credits on repeated scans. Rate limit: respect API limits.

- [x] t216 Orphaned PR scanner — run eagerly after worker evaluation, not just Phase 6 throttled #bugfix #supervisor #self-improvement ~1.5h (ai:1h test:30m) ref:GH#911 assignee:marcusquinn started:2026-02-10T04:36:28Z logged:2026-02-10 completed:2026-02-10 pr:#917
  - Notes: Currently scan_orphaned_prs() only runs in Phase 6 of the pulse with a 10-minute throttle. Workers that create PRs but get evaluated as `task_only` (because the PR wasn't in the DB) must wait for the next throttle window. Fix: (1) After any worker evaluates as `complete (task_only)`, immediately check GitHub for open PRs on that task's branch (`feature/tXXX`) — this is a targeted single-PR lookup, not a full scan, so no throttle needed. (2) If found, link the PR and transition to `pr_review` instead of `deployed`. (3) Keep the full Phase 6 scan as a safety net for edge cases. This eliminates the gap where t204 created PR #886 but the supervisor marked it `deployed (task_only)`.

- [x] t217 Worker prompt — enforce Task tool parallelism for independent subtasks #enhancement #supervisor #efficiency ~1h (ai:45m test:15m) ref:GH#912 assignee:marcusquinn started:2026-02-10T04:37:10Z logged:2026-02-10 completed:2026-02-10 pr:#918
  - Notes: Workers currently receive a suggestion to use the Task tool for parallel sub-work (line 3649 of supervisor-helper.sh) but none actually do it — all 4 workers in backlog-12 executed sequentially. Strengthen the prompt: (1) Change from suggestion to explicit instruction with a concrete example. (2) Add a decision heuristic: "If your TodoWrite has 3+ subtasks and any two don't modify the same files, spawn the independent one via Task tool." (3) Add a worked example showing how to parallelise (e.g., writing tests in a sub-agent while implementing the main script). (4) Track whether workers actually use Task tool in evaluation — add a heuristic check for `mcp_task` calls in the log.

- [x] t218 Verification proof-logs — structured audit trail for task completion trust #enhancement #supervisor #verification ~2h (ai:1.5h test:30m) ref:GH#913 assignee:marcusquinn started:2026-02-10T04:38:00Z logged:2026-02-10 completed:2026-02-10 pr:#921
  - Notes: The verify stage (t180) runs check: directives from VERIFY.md but doesn't produce a structured proof-log that can be audited later. Without proof-logs, false completions (task_only, no_pr) are hard to diagnose and trust. Implement: (1) Create a `proof-log.json` per task in `$SUPERVISOR_DIR/proofs/tXXX.json` containing: task_id, pr_url, pr_merged_at, ci_checks (name+status), review_triage_result, verify_checks (each check: directive + pass/fail + output snippet), deploy_confirmed (setup.sh exit code), todo_updated_at. (2) The supervisor writes to this log at each lifecycle stage (pr_review, merging, deploying, verifying). (3) `update_todo_on_complete()` must refuse to mark `[x]` unless proof-log exists and all stages passed. (4) Add `supervisor-helper.sh proof <task_id>` command to display the proof-log for any task. (5) Add `supervisor-helper.sh audit [batch_id]` to summarise proof-logs for a batch — flag any tasks marked complete without full proof chain.

- [x] t219 PR lifecycle — faster merge pipeline with parallel CI + review triage #enhancement #supervisor #throughput ~1.5h (ai:1h test:30m) ref:GH#914 assignee:marcusquinn started:2026-02-10T04:39:17Z logged:2026-02-10 completed:2026-02-10 pr:#922
  - Notes: The PR lifecycle (pr_review → review_triage → merging → merged → deploying → deployed) processes one stage per pulse (every 5 min). A PR with passing CI and no review threads takes 3+ pulses (15+ min) to go from complete to deployed. Improve: (1) Allow multi-stage transitions within a single pulse — if CI passes and no review threads, go straight from pr_review to merging in one pulse. (2) After merge, immediately run deploy + verify in the same pulse instead of waiting for the next one. (3) Add a fast-path: if the PR has all CI green and zero review comments at evaluation time, skip the pr_review wait and go directly to merging. (4) Log timing metrics per stage in the proof-log (t218) so we can measure pipeline latency and identify bottlenecks.

- [x] t1124 Skip markdown code-fenced lines in TODO.md parser #bugfix #git #sync #auto-dispatch ~30m model:sonnet ref:GH#1682 assignee:marcusquinn started:2026-02-18T16:28:50Z logged:2026-02-18 pr:#1692 verified:2026-02-18
  - issue-sync-helper.sh grep patterns (`^\s*- \[ \] t[0-9]+`) match task-like lines inside markdown code blocks (` ` ```)
  - This creates phantom issues from format examples in TODO.md (e.g. `- [ ] t001 Task description @owner`)
  - Discovered in a managed project repo: format section had example tasks that collided with real task IDs, creating duplicate/wrong GitHub issues
  - Workaround applied: renamed examples to `tXXX`/`tYYY`/`tZZZ` placeholders
  - Proper fix: add a code-fence-aware filter before task extraction — track ``` state and skip lines inside fenced blocks
  - Affects: `cmd_push`, `cmd_close`, `cmd_pull`, `cmd_enrich`, `cmd_status`, `cmd_reconcile` — all use the same grep pattern
  - Simplest approach: a shared `extract_tasks()` function that pipes TODO.md through an awk filter stripping code blocks before grep

- [x] t1125 Fix jq JSON parsing errors in supervisor action executor pipeline #bugfix #auto-dispatch #self-improvement ~1h model:sonnet category:automation — The supervisor action executor has recurring jq compile errors: 'syntax error, unexpected LITERAL', 'May need parentheses around object key expression', 'invalid JSON text passed to --argjson'. These cause rc=1 pipeline errors that silently drop valid actions. Root cause is likely unescaped quotes or special characters in JSON fields (e.g., task descriptions with apostrophes) being passed to jq --argjson. - [x] t1179 Add cycle-aware dedup to supervisor — skip targets acted on in previous cycle unless state changed #enhancement #auto-dispatch #self-improvement ~2h model:sonnet category:automation — Self-reflection shows 13 targets receiving repeated actions across 5 cycles. Several are already-completed tasks (t1143, t1142, t1125) or issues already addressed by merged PRs (t1144 resolved the audit findings for #1695, #1572). This is distinct from t1138 (which adds general dedup) — this specifically addresses the cycle-over-cycle repetition pattern visible in self-reflection data.
